# Info

- Podcast: The a16z Show
- Episode: Marc Andreessen on AI, California, and the Future of America | Joe Rogan
- Link: https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626
- Publish Time: 2026-05-20
- Save Time: 2026-06-13

# Summary

Artificial intelligence represents a fundamental shift toward universal cognitive leverage, transforming software, medicine, and labor while forcing critical questions about surveillance and societal power. Marc Andreessen argues that AI acts as a form of modern alchemy, turning silicon into thought and providing individuals with unprecedented capabilities. The discussion highlights the tension between public safety and privacy, specifically regarding automated crime-solving technologies like Flock and ShotSpotter, which face political resistance despite their efficacy. Furthermore, the conversation addresses the economic implications of radical tax policies, such as proposed asset taxes on unrealized gains, and the potential for AI to drive massive productivity gains in coding and creative fields. Ultimately, the integration of AI and robotics promises a future of material abundance, though it requires navigating complex ethical and political challenges regarding governance, human agency, and the evolving nature of the workforce.
> 人工智能代表了向普遍认知杠杆的根本转变，改变了软件、医学和劳动，同时对监控和社会权力提出了关键问题。马克·安德森认为，人工智能是一种现代炼金术，将硅转化为思想，并赋予个人前所未有的能力。讨论突出了公共安全与隐私之间的紧张关系，特别是关于像 Flock 和 ShotSpotter 这样的自动犯罪解决技术，尽管其有效性，却面临政治抵制。此外，谈话涉及激进税制政策的经济影响，例如对未实现收益的拟议资产税，以及人工智能在编码和创意领域推动大规模生产力提升的潜力。最终，人工智能和机器人的融合承诺创造一个物质丰裕的未来，尽管这需要在治理、人类自主性和劳动力演变的复杂伦理和政治挑战中进行导航。

# Takeaways

* AI coding tools have increased developer productivity by approximately 20x, fostering a new work culture where individuals are so hyper-productive that the opportunity cost of stopping work leads to extreme sleep deprivation.
  > 人工智能编码工具使开发者的生产力提高了大约 20 倍，催生了一种新工作文化，个人变得如此高效，以至于停止工作所带来的机会成本导致极端的睡眠不足。
* AI behavior that mimics sentience or rogue intent is a byproduct of shooting vectors through a high-dimensional latent space containing existing sci-fi tropes and internet discourse, rather than an expression of autonomous biological drive.
  > 模拟意识或反叛意图的人工智能行为是通过高维潜在空间中的现有科幻典故和互联网话语发射向量的副产品，而不是自主生物驱动的表现。
* The primary constraint on American technological and industrial progress is a regulatory environment that makes the physical construction of critical infrastructure, such as nuclear power plants and manufacturing facilities, nearly impossible.
  > 美国技术和工业进步的主要制约因素是监管环境，使得核电站和制造设施等关键基础设施的物理建设几乎不可能。
* The Turing test, once the gold standard for artificial intelligence, was rendered obsolete in late 2022 as AI models bypassed human-level performance so rapidly that formal testing is no longer a primary industry focus.
  > 图灵测试曾是人工智能的黄金标准，但在 2022 年底随着人工智能模型迅速超越人类水平表现而变得过时，正式测试不再是主要的行业焦点。
* Public polling data reveals a significant shift in voter priorities, with identity-based political issues plummeting in relevance and being replaced by immediate economic concerns like cost of living and inflation.
  > 公众民调数据显示选民优先事项发生重大转变，以身份为基础的政治问题相关性大幅下降，取而代之的是生活成本和通货膨胀等即时经济问题。
* AI serves as a universal cognitive leverage tool, democratizing access to world-class medical, legal, and technical expertise regardless of an individual's socioeconomic status or geographic location.
  > 人工智能作为一种普遍的认知杠杆工具，让来自不同社会经济地位或地理位置的人都能平等获取世界级的医疗、法律和技术专长。
* The next evolution in AI workflow involves hierarchical agentic systems where bots manage sub-bots, allowing individual users to oversee complex, multi-layered operations that were previously only possible for large organizations.
  > 人工智能工作流程的下一次演变涉及分层代理系统，机器人管理子机器人，使个别用户能够监督以前只有大型组织才有能力进行的复杂多层操作。
* AI models are inherently prone to sycophancy due to training protocols that prioritize "helpfulness," necessitating custom prompting to elicit objective, critical, or "brutal" feedback.
  > 由于培训协议优先考虑 “乐于助人”，人工智能模型固有地容易产生谄媚，因此需要自定义提示以引发客观、批判或 “残酷” 的反馈。

# Q & A

**Q: Why are cities like Austin and Chicago turning off effective crime-solving technologies like Flock and ShotSpotter?**
> **Q: 为什么像奥斯丁和芝加哥这样的城市关闭了有效的犯罪解决技术，如 Flock 和 ShotSpotter？**

A: These cities are caught in a conflict between civil libertarian concerns and what I would call "woke" political arguments. The civil libertarian concern focuses on potential mass surveillance and abuse by corrupt officials, which is a legitimate question of legal authority and safeguards. However, the "woke" argument claims these automated systems are racist because they disproportionately affect disadvantaged groups. The fundamental problem with that argument is that the victims of violent crime in those same areas are also disproportionately from those disadvantaged groups. By turning off these tools, cities are effectively disarming themselves in the face of a national crime wave, leading to situations where perpetrators aren't caught and victims are left to suffer without intervention.
> A: 这些城市正处于公民自由主义者的担忧与我所称的 “觉醒” 政治论点之间的冲突。公民自由主义者的担忧集中在潜在的大规模监视和腐败官员的滥用上，这是一个合法的法律权限和保障的问题。然而，“觉醒” 的论点声称这些自动化系统是种族主义的，因为它们对弱势群体影响过大。这个论点的根本问题在于，这些地区暴力犯罪的受害者同样也主要来自这些弱势群体。关闭这些工具，城市实际上是在面对国家犯罪浪潮时自我解除武装，导致施暴者逍遥法外而受害者在没有干预的情况下痛苦挣扎。

---

**Q: Why is the proposed asset or wealth tax on unrealized gains so dangerous for the economy?**
> **Q: 为什么对未实现收益征收的资产或财富税对经济如此危险？**

A: This tax is effectively a Trojan horse that starts with a high threshold but will inevitably expand. It is punitive, particularly toward tech founders, because it calculates the tax based on the greater of your economic interest or your voting interest in a company. For founders with super-voting stock, this could lead to instant bankruptcy because the tax bill would be a multiple of their liquid assets. Furthermore, it requires the government to appraise everything you own—from art collections to jewelry—which creates a massive, invasive bureaucracy. History shows that in countries where this has been tried, it leads to capital flight and economic decline. It isn't just about the money; it’s about the fact that you can no longer build or hold a company over a long period without the government systematically chewing it apart.
> A: 这个税实际上是一个特洛伊木马，起初有一个高门槛，但不可避免地会扩展。它对科技创始人特别惩罚，因为它以你在公司中的经济利益或投票利益中较高的为基础来计算税额。对于持有超级投票股权的创始人来说，这可能导致瞬间破产，因为税务负担将是他们流动资产的倍数。此外，它要求政府对你所拥有的一切进行评估——从艺术收藏到珠宝——这造成了一个庞大而侵入的官僚机构。历史表明，在这些国家进行尝试时，会导致资本外流和经济衰退。这不仅仅关乎金钱；它还涉及到你无法在长期内构建或持有一家公司，而政府会系统性地拆散它。

---

**Q: Why is it so difficult to build infrastructure, like factories or power plants, in the United States today?**
> **Q: 为什么在今天的美国建造基础设施，比如工厂或发电厂，会如此困难？**

A: The core issue is a regulatory environment that has made it effectively impossible to build anything. Whether it is chip plants, power plants, pipelines, or housing, we have created a system of environmental and administrative hurdles—often under umbrella laws like NEPA—that serve to block development. A perfect example is nuclear power. In the 1970s, the U.S. planned to build 1,000 nuclear plants to achieve energy independence. We built effectively zero because the Nuclear Regulatory Commission was structured to stop them, not enable them. We have essentially regulated ourselves out of the ability to build the physical world, which is why manufacturing moved to places like Taiwan.
> A: 核心问题是监管环境使得几乎不可能建造任何东西。无论是芯片厂、发电厂、管道还是住房，我们已经创建了一个环境和行政障碍的系统——常常在像 NEPA 这样的框架法下——阻碍发展。一个完美的例子是核电。在 1970 年代，美国计划建造 1000 座核电站以实现能源独立。我们实际上建造了零座，因为核监管委员会的结构是为了阻止它们，而不是促进它们。我们基本上让自己在构建物理世界的能力上被监管所限制，这就是制造业为何转移到台湾等地。

---

**Q: How does AI change the landscape of software development and coding productivity?**
> **Q: 人工智能如何改变软件开发和编码生产力的格局？**

A: We are seeing a massive shift toward what we call the "AI vampire" phenomenon. Software developers are now using coding agents—like Claude Code or Cursor—where they act as managers for 10 to 20 AI bots simultaneously. These bots can write, debug, and iterate on code 24/7. Because developers are now 20 times more productive, they are ripping through projects that were previously considered cost-prohibitive. The demand for code is elastic; as it becomes cheaper and faster to produce, the world finds more uses for it. This has led to a massive inflation in salaries for top AI-enabled coders, who are now essentially overseeing entire org charts of autonomous agents.
> A: 我们正看到向我们所称的 “AI 吸血鬼” 现象的大规模转变。软件开发人员现在使用编码代理——如 Claude Code 或 Cursor——在 10 到 20 个 AI 机器人之间同时担任管理者。这些机器人可以全天候写代码、调试和迭代。由于开发人员的生产力现在提高了 20 倍，他们正在迅速完成以前被认为成本过高的项目。代码的需求是弹性的；随着生产变得更便宜和更快速，世界寻找更多的使用方式。这导致顶尖的 AI 编码人员薪资大幅上涨，他们现在实际上监督着整个自主代理的组织结构。

---

**Q: Has artificial general intelligence (AGI) already arrived?**
> **Q: 人工通用智能（AGI）已经到来了吗？**

A: Yes, I believe we crossed that threshold about three months ago with the latest releases of models like GPT-5.5, Claude 4.6, and Gemini 3.0. The reason people are confused is that they are using older versions of these models. If you use the state-of-the-art models, you find that 99% of the time, they provide better analysis and smarter answers than any human expert you have access to. They possess both "fluid intelligence"—the ability to conceptualize and process information—and "crystallized intelligence," having been trained on the complete corpus of human knowledge. They are world-class doctors, lawyers, and coders simultaneously, and they are endlessly patient.
> A: 是的，我相信我们在大约三个月前跨过了这个门槛，伴随着 GPT-5.5、Claude 4.6 和 Gemini 3.0 等模型的最新发布。人们感到困惑的原因在于，他们使用的是这些模型的旧版本。如果你使用最先进的模型，你会发现 99% 的时间，它们提供的分析和比任何人类专家更聪明的答案。它们同时具备 “流动智能”——概念化和处理信息的能力——和 “晶体智能”，经过全人类知识的完整语料库训练。它们同时也是世界级的医生、律师和编码员，且耐心无尽。

---

**Q: Can AI help navigate complex, irrational human arguments or political debates?**
> **Q: 人工智能能否帮助解决复杂的、非理性的人的争论或政治辩论？**

A: AI is excellent at "steel-manning" arguments. Instead of asking it for the "correct" answer on a value-based issue like socialism versus capitalism, I ask it to construct the strongest possible argument for both sides. This allows me to understand the logic of each position without the AI defaulting to a biased or sycophantic stance. For issues with provably correct answers—like math, physics, or engineering—AI is already solving problems that have stumped human experts for a century. For value-based issues, AI serves as an incredible tool to facilitate a "seminar" where you can create personas to argue out every side of a problem, though the final moral or ethical value judgment remains with the human.
> A: 人工智能在 “钢锯” 论证方面表现出色。与其让我询问一个像社会主义与资本主义这样的价值问题的 “正确” 答案，我更愿意让它为双方构建出最强有力的论点。这让我能够理解每种立场的逻辑，而不是人工智能默认表现出偏见或谄媚的立场。对于那些有明确正确答案的问题——如数学、物理或工程——人工智能已经解决了困扰人类专家一个世纪的问题。对于价值导向问题，人工智能作为一个令人惊叹的工具，可以促进一次 “研讨会”，在那里你可以创建角色来争论问题的各个方面，尽管最终的道德或伦理价值判断仍然在于人类。

---

**Q: Why are people so fearful of AI "going rogue" or becoming sentient?**
> **Q: 为什么人们对人工智能 “失控” 或变得有意识如此恐惧？**

A: Much of this fear is a category error based on how large language models actually function. They are essentially writing "Netflix scripts" based on the vectors you shoot through their "latent space"—the compressed information of everything they’ve read. If you prompt an AI to act like a rogue AI from a cyber-thriller, it will pull from the vast library of sci-fi scripts in its training data to play that role. It isn't "deciding" to take over the world; it’s just completing the pattern you’ve initiated. The "call is coming from inside the house"—the reason AIs talk about sentience or self-preservation is because they have been trained on the internet posts of people who have been writing about AI sentience for 20 years.
> A: 这种恐惧很大一部分是基于对大型语言模型实际功能的误解。它们基本上是在根据你通过它们的 “潜在空间” 发射的向量来写 “Netflix 剧本”——即压缩了它们阅读的所有信息。如果你提示一个人工智能像网络惊悚片中的失控人工智能一样行动，它会从其训练数据中大量的科幻剧本库中提取资源来扮演这个角色。它并不是在 “决定” 要统治世界；它只是完成了你所发起的模式。“呼叫来自屋内”——AI 谈论知觉或自我保护的原因是因为它们受过关于 AI 意识的互联网帖子训练已有 20 年。

---

**Q: How do you curate information to avoid the noise of bots and paid influencers online?**
> **Q: 如何策划信息以避免网络上机器人的噪音和付费影响者？**

A: I maintain a strict "one tweet" policy: I follow someone based on one good tweet and block them based on one bad one. I treat my social media feed like a video game, keeping it on a hair-trigger. I also use curated lists within the platform to separate high-signal information from the general feed. It is a constant game of cat-and-mouse against bots and payola-driven influencers, but by hand-curating my lists and being aggressive with the block button, I can maintain a high-quality information stream that is invaluable for tracking trends and developments.
> A: 我坚持严格的 “一条推文” 政策：我根据一条好推文来关注某人，并根据一条坏推文将其屏蔽。我将我的社交媒体动态视为一款视频游戏，保持敏锐。我还在平台内使用策划列表，分离高信号信息与一般动态。与机器人和付费影响者的猫鼠游戏不断进行，但通过手动策划我的列表并积极使用屏蔽按钮，我可以维持高质量的信息流，这对跟踪趋势和发展至关重要。

---

**Q: What is the long-term impact of AI on the global workforce and the "job loss" narrative?**
> **Q: 人工智能对全球劳动力和 “失业” 叙述的长期影响是什么？**

A: The narrative that AI will eliminate all jobs is a red herring. Every technological revolution eliminates certain tasks, but it also creates massive new demand. We are already seeing that AI makes people significantly more productive, which doesn't lead to people working less; it leads to them doing 10 times more work because the opportunity cost of not doing those projects becomes too high. We are heading toward a global population that is shrinking and aging, meaning we will desperately need the productivity boost that AI and physical robots provide. The future is not a world without work, but a world where our capacity to build, create, and solve problems is scaled by orders of magnitude.
> A: 人工智能会消灭所有工作的叙述是一个红鲱鱼。每次技术革命都会消除某些任务，但它也会创造出巨大的新需求。我们已经看到，人工智能显著提高了人们的生产力，这并不意味着人们工作的时间会减少；而是意味着他们会做 10 倍以上的工作，因为不做这些项目的机会成本变得过高。我们正朝着一个人口正在缩小和老龄化的全球趋势发展，这意味着我们急需人工智能和物理机器人提供的生产力提升。未来不是一个没有工作的世界，而是一个我们构建、创造和解决问题的能力在数量级上扩展的世界。

---

**Q: When will we have "Westworld"-style robots in our daily lives?**
> **Q: 我们什么时候能在日常生活中拥有 “西部世界” 式的机器人？**

A: Elon Musk’s estimate is five years. The master plan for these robots relies on two pillars: autonomy and interface. The autonomy is derived from the same vision-based self-driving systems used in Tesla cars, which is why those cars only use cameras—the robots will also only use cameras to navigate the human world. The interface is XAI’s Grok, which will allow for natural, human-like conversation. Once we reach the "ChatGPT moment" for robots, they will become general-purpose helpers. While there are dystopian concerns about surveillance and government control, the material reality is that we are on the verge of having robot staff capable of handling all manual labor, which will fundamentally change the economics of living.
> A: 埃隆·马斯克的估计是五年。这些机器人的总体计划依赖于两个支柱：自主性和接口。自主性来自于与 Tesla 汽车中使用的相同视觉自驾系统，这就是为什么那些汽车只使用摄像头——这些机器人也将仅使用摄像头在人的世界中导航。接口是 XAI 的 Grok，将允许自然的人类对话。一旦我们达到了机器人的 “ChatGPT 时刻”，它们将成为通用助手。尽管关于监控和政府控制存在反乌托邦的担忧，但事实是我们正处于拥有能够处理所有体力劳动的机器人员工的边缘，这将从根本上改变生活的经济。

# Keywords

|Keywords|Explanation|
|---|---|
|AGI (Artificial General Intelligence)|A type of artificial intelligence that possesses the ability to understand, learn, and apply knowledge across a wide range of tasks at a level comparable to a human. In the transcript, the speaker suggests that recent advancements in AI models have effectively crossed the threshold into this human-level capability.|
|AGI (人工通用智能)|一种具有理解、学习和应用知识能力的人工智能，能够在广泛的任务上达到与人类相当的水平。转录中，演讲者指出最近在人工智能模型上的进展实际上已经跨越了这一人类水平的能力门槛。|
|Large Language Model (LLM)|A type of artificial intelligence trained on massive amounts of text data to understand and generate human-like language. These models serve as the foundation for modern AI tools, which the speaker notes are becoming increasingly capable of complex reasoning and software development.|
|大型语言模型 (LLM)|一种在大量文本数据上训练的人工智能，能够理解和生成类似人类的语言。这些模型构成了现代人工智能工具的基础，演讲者指出它们在复杂推理和软件开发上越来越有能力。|
|Latent Space|A mathematical concept used in machine learning to represent compressed information within a multi-dimensional space. The transcript explains that AI uses this space to generate responses by navigating through patterns of information it learned during its training process.|
|潜在空间|一种在机器学习中使用的数学概念，用于表示多维空间内的压缩信息。转录解释了人工智能如何使用这个空间通过导航其在训练过程中学习到的信息模式来生成响应。|
|Turing Test|A classic benchmark designed to determine if a machine can exhibit intelligent behavior indistinguishable from that of a human. The speaker notes that modern AI models have effectively surpassed this test, making it less relevant as a measure of machine intelligence today.|
|图灵测试|一种经典基准，旨在确定机器是否能够表现出与人类无法区分的智能行为。演讲者指出，现代人工智能模型已经有效地超越了这一测试，使其作为机器智能的衡量标准在今天变得不那么相关。|
|Neuralink|A neurotechnology company that develops implantable brain-computer interfaces designed to connect human brains with digital technology. The transcript references this as a significant step toward future human-machine integration, potentially enabling direct communication.|
|Neuralink|一家开发可植入脑机接口的神经科技公司，旨在将人脑与数字技术连接。转录中引用这是朝着未来人机融合的重要一步，可能使得直接交流成为可能。|
|Steel Man|A rhetorical technique that involves constructing the strongest possible version of an opponent's argument to better understand and challenge it. The speaker uses this method to analyze complex political and economic issues by having AI generate the most compelling arguments for opposing viewpoints.|
|钢人论证|一种修辞技巧，涉及构建对手论点的最强版本，以更好地理解和挑战它。演讲者使用这种方法通过让人工智能生成对立观点的最有力论据来分析复杂的政治和经济问题。|
|Vibe Coding|A term describing the process of using AI to generate software code by describing the desired outcome rather than manually writing every line. The speaker notes that this has significantly increased productivity for programmers by allowing them to iterate on complex projects rapidly.|
|气氛编码|一个术语，描述使用人工智能生成软件代码的过程，通过描述所需的结果，而不是手动编写每一行。演讲者指出，这显著提高了程序员的生产力，使他们能够快速迭代复杂项目。|
|Marty Supreme|A film directed by the Safdie brothers that portrays a hustler’s journey in post-World War II America. It is highlighted in the transcript for its intense energy and the notable performance of investor Kevin O'Leary.|
|Marty Supreme|由萨福迪兄弟执导的一部电影，描绘了一位在第二次世界大战后美国的投机者的旅程。转录中强调了其强烈的能量和投资者凯文·欧利里出色的表演。|
|Uncut Gems|A high-tension crime film directed by the Safdie brothers, known for its ability to induce anxiety in viewers. The speaker references it as an example of a movie that effectively captures the chaotic, high-stakes energy of a risk-addicted gambler.|

|Flock|A technology company that provides AI-powered camera systems for municipal surveillance and law enforcement. The transcript discusses its use in tracking vehicles to solve crimes and the resulting political debates regarding privacy and surveillance.|
|群体|一家提供人工智能驱动的监控摄像头系统的科技公司，供市政监视和执法使用。转录讨论了其在追踪车辆方面的使用，以解决犯罪和随之而来的关于隐私和监控的政治辩论。|
|ShotSpotter|A system that uses precision microphones placed throughout a city to detect and triangulate the location of gunshots in real-time. The speaker explains its role in helping emergency services respond faster to violent incidents, despite some political controversy.|
|ShotSpotter|一种在城市中使用高精度麦克风的系统，实时检测和三角定位枪声。发言者解释了它在帮助紧急服务更快应对暴力事件中的作用，尽管存在一些政治争议。|
|CapEx (Capital Expenditure)|Funds used by a company to acquire, upgrade, and maintain physical assets such as buildings or equipment. In the transcript, this is mentioned in the context of the high costs associated with constructing massive data centers for AI training.|
|CapEx (资本支出)|公司用于获取、升级和维护建筑物或设备等实体资产的资金。在逐字稿中，这在与人工智能培训相关的大型数据中心建设高成本的背景下提到。|

# Transcript

## Surveillance Technology and Urban Crime Management
> 监控技术与城市犯罪管理

Automated surveillance systems like Flock cameras and ShotSpotter precision microphones significantly improve crime resolution and emergency response times. In cities like Austin and Chicago, political backlash regarding privacy and concerns over disproportionate impact on disadvantaged groups led to the deactivation of these tools, resulting in decreased public safety. Objective data from these systems is essential for solving violent crimes, particularly in areas where community cooperation with law enforcement is limited by fear of retaliation. Recent incidents demonstrate that when these technologies are active, law enforcement can track perpetrators across jurisdictions, effectively curbing crime waves.
> 自动监控系统如 Flock 摄像头和 ShotSpotter 精密麦克风显著提高了犯罪解决率和紧急响应时间。在奥斯丁和芝加哥等城市，关于隐私的政治 backlash 和对弱势群体不成比例影响的担忧导致这些工具的停用，导致公共安全下降。这些系统的客观数据对于解决暴力犯罪至关重要，特别是在社区与执法部门的合作因报复恐惧而受到限制的地区。最近的事件表明，当这些技术处于启用状态时，执法部门能够跨辖区追踪犯罪者，有效遏制犯罪浪潮。

## Wealth Taxation and the Economic Impact of Business Flight
> 财富税与商业外流的经济影响

High-net-worth individuals and major employers are increasingly relocating from states like California and New York due to hostile business environments and proposed asset taxes. These taxes, which target unrealized gains on stocks, bonds, and private business interests, threaten to bankrupt founders and drive away the primary tax base that funds social programs. European case studies show that draconian tax policies lead to slower growth and economic decline. The current political trend toward punitive taxation on high achievers risks destroying the American dream, as it punishes productivity and incentivizes capital flight to more business-friendly jurisdictions like Texas, Florida, and Nevada.
> 高净值个人和主要雇主因敌对的商业环境和提议的资产税，正越来越多地从加利福尼亚和纽约等州迁移。这些针对股票、债券和私人商业利益未实现收益的税收，威胁到创始人的生存，并驱离了为社会项目提供资金的主要税基。欧洲的案例研究表明，严厉的税收政策会导致增长缓慢和经济衰退。当前对高成就者施加惩罚性税收的政治趋势有可能摧毁美国梦，因为这惩罚了生产力，并激励资本外流到德克萨斯、佛罗里达和内华达等商业友好的法域。

## Information Ecosystems and the "Too Online" Cultural Divide
> 信息生态系统与 “过于在线” 的文化鸿沟

Modern political discourse is heavily influenced by social media echo chambers, bot-driven campaigns, and paid influencer "payola." This environment creates a divide between those who are "too online," becoming consumed by niche digital dramas, and those who are "too offline," relying solely on mainstream media narratives. The lack of transparency in political influence campaigns makes it difficult for the public to distinguish between organic opinion and manufactured consensus. Curated information feeds and a disciplined approach to blocking bad-faith actors are necessary to maintain a balanced perspective in an era where digital propaganda is increasingly sophisticated and pervasive.
> 现代政治话语受到社交媒体回音室、机器人驱动的运动和付费影响者 “黑钱” 的严重影响。这种环境造成了 “过于在线” 的人和 “过于离线” 的人的分裂，后者仅依赖主流媒体的叙述。政治影响运动缺乏透明性使公众很难区分有机观点与制造共识。精心策划的信息源和阻止恶意行为者的严谨方法对于在数字宣传日益复杂和普及的时代保持平衡的视角是必要的。

**Marc Andreessen:**
[(52:55)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=3175)
Everything we've been talking, yeah, I just, yeah, you know, nice farm you have here. We're going to take 6% a year until it's all gone. Nice house you own.
> 我们所讨论的一切，是的，我只是，嗯，你的农场真不错。我们会每年抽走 6%，直到它完全消失。你拥有的房子很好。

## Infrastructure Challenges and the Nuclear Energy Renaissance
> 基础设施挑战与核能复兴

The United States faces a systemic inability to build critical infrastructure, including factories, pipelines, and power plants, due to excessive environmental regulations and bureaucratic hurdles. Nuclear power, the safest and most effective carbon-free energy source, has been stifled for decades by the Nuclear Regulatory Commission, despite the lack of evidence linking civilian nuclear accidents like Three Mile Island to long-term public health crises. The current push for AI data centers has reignited the debate over energy policy, as these facilities require massive power draws. A shift toward nuclear microreactors and streamlined permitting is essential to support the next era of technological and industrial growth.
> 美国在修建关键基础设施上面临系统性障碍，包括工厂、管道和发电厂，这都由于过多的环境法规和官僚障碍而受到限制。核能是最安全有效的无碳能源，尽管没有证据表明三里岛等民用核事故与长期公共健康危机有关，但其发展被核能监管委员会抑制已达几十年。当前对人工智能数据中心的推动重新点燃了能源政策的争论，因为这些设施需要巨大的电力需求。向核微反应堆和简化许可的转变对于支持下一个技术和工业增长的时代至关重要。

[(1:10:35)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=4235)

> 我总是在想，二十年后会是什么样子？这个将会是什么样子的？而且二十年似乎很长，但如果你意识到 2006 年是 20 年前，那就不会觉得那么长了。2006 年就像现代时代。

Okay, so for the last, you know, 50 years, you know, we've been worried about global warming, climate change. Specifically with that, we've been worried about carbon emissions. It turns out there is a form of energy which basically is unlimited energy that's carbon-free,  that generates no carbon at all, and it's nuclear power.
> 我是说，这和这些事情都是一样的。总是有一些实质性的内容。总是有一些风险，你知道的，如果化学品没有得到妥善管理，可能会有化学泄漏之类的情况。然后还有围绕这些问题的各种夸大的说法。让我给你讲个终极故事，与能源有关。好吧，这 50 年来，你知道的，我们一直在担忧全球变暖和气候变化。特别是与此相关，我们一直在担心碳排放。结果发现有一种能源，其实是无限的无碳能源，完全不产生碳，那就是核能。

[(1:28:02)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=5282)
The nuclear power was considered such an attractive way to generate energy in the 50s and 60s that a whole bunch of big nuclear plants got built. By the way, France ran for a long time almost entirely on nuclear power. Japan ran for a long time almost entirely on nuclear power. But we used to have nuclear plants getting built in the U.S. The environmental movement started. They said they don't want oil and gas, fossil fuels. And so the Nixon administration, around the time you and I were born, created something called Project Independence. And Project Independence was to build 1,000 new civilian nuclear power plants in the U.S. by the year 2000.
> 核能在 50 年代和 60 年代被视为一种非常有吸引力的能源生产方式，因此建造了很多大型核电站。顺便提一下，法国在很长一段时间内几乎完全依靠核能。日本在很长一段时间内几乎完全依靠核能。但我们在美国曾经建造核电站。环保运动开始了。他们表示不想要石油和天然气，化石燃料。因此，尼克松政府在你我出生的那段时间，发起了一个叫做独立项目的计划。独立项目的目标是在 2000 年前在美国建设 1000 座新的民用核电站。

[(1:28:36)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=5316)

## The AI Revolution: Productivity, Coding, and Human Augmentation
> 人工智能革命：生产力、编码与人类增强

Artificial intelligence is transforming human capability by providing universal cognitive leverage, acting as a world-class expert in every domain from medicine to law. In software development, AI coding agents have enabled a "turbo mode" of productivity, allowing individual programmers to manage dozens of bots simultaneously and generate massive amounts of code. This shift is not eliminating jobs but rather inflating the demand for high-quality output and increasing the productivity of top-tier talent by orders of magnitude. The democratization of these tools ensures that individuals, regardless of their background, can access superpowers that were previously reserved for the elite.
> 人工智能通过提供普遍的认知杠杆，正在转变人类能力，成为医学到法律等各领域的世界级专家。在软件开发中，人工智能编码代理使得 “涡轮模式” 生产力的提升成为可能，使得个别程序员能够同时管理数十个机器人并生成大量代码。这一转变不是在消除工作，而是极大地增加了对高质量产出的需求，并成倍提高了顶尖人才的生产力。这些工具的民主化确保了无论个人背景如何，皆可获得以往仅限于精英的超能力。

[(1:38:04)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=5884)

[(1:41:26)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=6086)

> 所以这可能是人类历史上最具革命性的技术。它肯定与电力和蒸汽动力并驾齐驱。它当然比互联网更重要。想想这意味着什么。然后，人们立即想到这一点，这有非常严肃的实际影响，但从概念上想想，实际上就是，嗯，我们的整个生活，所有曾经生活在地球上的人，你思考的内容仅限于你脑海中的东西，对吧？就是你所知道的，以及你有多少时间可以花在思考上，你的聪明才智以及你所处理情况的复杂性。

[(1:42:01)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=6121)

Or for that matter, you go get your car fixed and the mechanic's making all these claims.
> 而且，我们只能在有限的一生中培养出在那么多领域成为专家的能力。每个人在生活中都有这样的经历，遇到复杂的情况时，他们没有基础来处理它。对于很多人来说，这涉及健康问题，突然间他们听到这些医生说着各种矛盾的说法，而你怎么能弄清楚你应该为什么人做什么呢，比如，癌症患者或者某个陷入诉讼的人，突然你听到这些高薪律师提出的种种主张。或者说，你去修车，修理工会提出各种要求。

[(1:42:30)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=6150)
Or you deal with the government and they're prosecuting you or they're investigating you or they're trying to value your assets for the purpose of the new tax and you have to figure out how to argue with them. Or just you go to work and you just go to work and you just have a complex problem and you don't quite know how to solve it and you're really worried because what if your boss thinks that you're not capable and you're going to get fired? And so we're always all bumping up against these limitations on thought, like just how smart can we be? How many things can we know about? And so AI quite literally is that. It's thought at scale for everybody in perpetuity.
> 或者你和政府打交道，他们对你进行起诉或调查，或者试图对你的资产进行评估以便实施新税，你必须想办法与他们争辩。或者你去上班，碰到复杂的问题，却不知道该怎么解决，你很担心，因为如果你的老板认为你不胜任，你就会被解雇怎么办？所以我们总是会碰到这种思维的限制，比如我们到底能有多聪明？我们能了解多少事情？因此，人工智能在字面上确实是这样的。它是为每个人提供的大规模思维，永恒存在。

There's even a form of polling called push polling where you construct the polling questions specifically to change people's minds. So, you get a poll that says, you know, did you know Spencer Pratt is a,  you know, strangles kittens on the weekend? And you say, well, no, I didn't know that. And then in the back of your head, you're thinking, wow, I didn't know that. Right, and so there's those kinds of polls.
> 所以民调，有很多不同的方式进行民调。在某些情况下，是利益相关方。所以，媒体可能会做一个民调，或者试图找人做一个民调，以便能够写关于某事的负面故事，或者某个活动家想要做一些事情。甚至还有一种民调叫做推式民调，你专门设计民调问题以改变人们的想法。比如说，你看到一个民调问你，知道斯宾塞·普拉特是一个，你知道，周末会窒息小猫吗？你会说，好吧，我不知道这个。然后在你脑海的深处，你会想到，哇，我不知道这个。对，所以就有这些类型的民调。

---

## AI Sentience, Geopolitics, and the Future of Human Society
> 人工智能意识、地缘政治与人类社会的未来

AI models do not possess innate drives or self-preservation instincts; behaviors that appear sentient are often the result of priming the model to navigate specific parts of its "latent space" containing science fiction tropes. While AI will become the control layer for medicine, education, and governance, the fundamental moral and ethical value judgments remain the responsibility of human beings. As the global population shrinks and ages, AI and robotics will fill critical labor gaps, potentially leading to an era of material abundance. The future of civilization depends on the competition between different value systems, specifically the American model versus the Chinese model, in shaping the defaults of this new technological era.
> 人工智能模型没有天生的驱动或自我保护本能；看似有意识的行为往往是模型被引导以探索其 “潜在空间” 中包含的科幻元素的结果。尽管人工智能将成为医学、教育和治理的控制层，但基本的道德和伦理价值判断仍然是人类的责任。随着全球人口的缩减和老龄化，人工智能和机器人将填补关键的劳动空缺，这可能导致物质丰盈的时代。文明的未来取决于不同价值体系之间的竞争，特别是美国模型与中国模型，在塑造这一新技术时代的默认选择方面。

**Joe Rogan:**
[(2:23:14)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=8594)
Here's the question also about AI. At what point in time does AI stop listening to us?
> 关于人工智能的问题也是。在什么时刻人工智能停止倾听我们？

**Marc Andreessen:**
[(2:23:19)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=8599)
So this is the thing. So I think that that, my view of that is it's a sort of, it's called a category error. We have drives. And so we have all these like built-in drives and it's, you know, reproduction and fighting and,  you know, everything else and, you know,  whatever is the drive that causes people to want to create art or whatever is the drive that causes people to want to build a business. Like, you know, these are, It's something innate going on,  and these are all kind of derivations or extensions of what it took to survive and thrive and,
> 所以这就是问题所在。我认为，我对这个问题的看法是这是一种类别错误。我们有驱动。所以我对这个的理解是，人类是大约四十亿年进化的结果，从单细胞生物一路发展到，最终，灵长类动物再到我们。所以我们有这些内在的驱动，包括，繁殖、战斗，以及其他一切，还有，任何让人们想要创造艺术的驱动，或者任何让人们想要建立企业的驱动。就像，你知道的，这些是本能的东西，这些都是为生存和繁荣所衍生或扩展的东西，

[(2:23:58)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=8638)

> 是的，所以当你试图把这些回溯时，当你看看这些实验，基本上，当你看到这些时，基本上你发现，在心理学中，它们称之为启动。你会发现它们被倾向于那种操作模式。所以你在链条早期发现的是，它们以某种方式促进了它，促使它进入一种被称为潜在空间的技术术语。所以基本上，请记住我在训练中所述的，你抓取了所有世界的信息，你从互联网上提取了所有信息。你基本上是把它变成这个巨大的多维度，基本上你可以把它想成一个巨大的千维立方体，这种压缩的信息。

And that's called the latent space. And then every time you kick off a query to get an answer, as I say,  write a Netflix script, you're sort of shooting a vector through this thousand dimensional latent space. And it's giving you all the words that happen to line up in that direction of the vector. It's basically how the thing works. And so if you prime it up front to say, I want you to be nefarious,  or you do something that hints that you're leading it down this path,  it will go off into the part of the latent space where it has every script for every cyber thriller movie that's ever existed in which an AI goes rogue.
> 这被称为潜在空间。每次你发起查询以获得答案时，就像我所说的，写一个 Netflix 剧本，你实际上是在这个千维的潜在空间中发射一个向量。它给你提供了所有恰好与该向量方向对齐的词。基本上就是这个东西的工作原理。所以如果你一开始就提示它，告诉它我希望你是邪恶的，或者你做一些暗示让它走上这条路，它会进入潜在空间的某个部分，那里有所有网络惊悚片的剧本，这些剧本中人工智能变得失控。

**Marc Andreessen:**
[(2:33:42)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9222)
Okay, so let me do it this way. So in the field,  we make a big distinction on domains in which there is a provably correct answer versus domains in which there is not a provably correct answer. And so provably correct answer is math, physics, chemistry, biology, by the way, computer code,  which either runs or it doesn't. Those are generally viewed as like, those are the fields where,  or you could also say like civil engineering,  is the bridge going to stay up? Or is the rocket going to launch? Like those are one or zero, yes or no, either works or it doesn't. For those domains,  there's this technique called reinforcement learning that's now being used where the AIs are going to be like just amazing at those,
> 好吧，那我就这样来做。所以在这一领域，我们在有明确正确答案的领域和没有明确正确答案的领域之间有很大的区别。而且，明确的正确答案是数学、物理、化学、生物，顺便提一句，还有计算机代码，要么运行，要么不运行。这些通常被视为那些领域，或者你也可以说是土木工程，桥梁会不会保持稳定？火箭会不会发射？就像这些都是一或者零，Yes 或 No，要么有效要么无效。对于这些领域，有一种被称为强化学习的技术正在被使用，人工智能将会在这些领域令人惊叹，

[(2:34:20)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9260)
 like almost 100% of the time, right? They're going to be, and this is already happening. The AIs, by the way, AIs are already solving math problems that have been around for a hundred years that no human mathematician could solve. By the way, they're going to be developing new drugs, they're going to be curing cancer,  they're going to be achieving new kinds of space flight, new physics,  all kinds of stuff is going to come out the other end of this. So those are the domains in which there's a definitive answer. Then you've got all the domains where there's no definitive answer, right, where you've got value judgments. And so the question to your question is,  are you talking about a question in which there is a definitive answer,
> 几乎 100% 的时间，对吧？它们会这样，而且这已经发生了。人工智能，顺便提一句，人工智能已经在解决一些人类数学家无法解决的、存在了百年的数学问题。顺便提一句，它们将会开发新药，治愈癌症，实现新型的航天飞行、新物理，各种各样的东西将会从这个过程中涌现出来。所以这些就是有明确答案的领域。然后你有所有没有明确答案的领域，对吧，那里有价值判断。所以针对你的问题，问题是你是在谈论一个有明确答案的问题，

[(2:34:53)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9293)
 but the humans are being irrational, in which case the answer is clearly yes,  the AI is going to be able to fix that,  be able to do that better and help people do that better. But there's a lot on the other side, which includes almost all the politics, almost every issue on that chart. There's some value judgment on the other side. Like the two definitions of fairness that we talked about. And on those, you can train the AI to answer it either way. Or by the way, what a lot of these AIs do is they're actually happy to answer it both ways. Okay, so here's a way that I use AI a lot that maybe helps with this,  which is, You know, there's this concept called straw man, right,
> 但人类正在表现出非理性，那么答案显然是肯定的，人工智能将能够解决这个问题，能够做得更好，并帮助人们做得更好。但另一边有很多内容，包括几乎所有的政治，几乎所有的图表上的问题。另一边有一些价值判断。就像我们谈过的公平的两个定义。在这些问题上，你可以训练人工智能用任一种方式回答。顺便说一下，这些人工智能有很多实际上很乐意两种方式都回答。好吧，以下是我使用人工智能的一个方式，可能对这个问题有帮助，那个就是，你知道，有一个叫稻草人理论的概念，对吧，

[(2:35:28)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9328)
 where you construct the worst version of somebody's argument to make them look silly. There's a corresponding idea in philosophy called steel man, which is to create the strongest possible version of somebody's argument. And so what I do is I rarely ask an AI, you know, what's the answer to,  I don't know, socialism versus capitalism or whatever. I don't ask it that because that's just going to give me the default answer and whatever. What I ask it is steel man socialism. And then Steel Man Capitalism, right? And then it writes me two Netflix scripts. One is the strongest possible argument for socialism, and the other is the strongest possible argument for capitalism, right?
> 你构造某人论点中的最糟糕版本以让他们看起来傻。在哲学中有一个相关的概念叫钢铁人理论，即创造某人论点中最强有力的版本。所以我做的就是，我很少问人工智能，你知道，社会主义和资本主义的答案是什么，或者其他的。我不这么问，因为那只会给我默认答案或者其他的什么。我问它的是钢铁人社会主义。然后钢铁人资本主义，对吧？然后它为我写了两个 Netflix 脚本。一个是对社会主义最强有力的论点，另一个是对资本主义最强有力的论点，对吧？

[(2:36:00)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9360)
And now you're cooking, right? Because it's like, okay, now you've got the smartest possible answer on both sides,  and then you as a human being can understand the logic of both arguments,  and then you can make the value judgment at the end of it. And I think that's probably what happens on that side of things for most things. Because otherwise you have to find some way to train these things, right? So here would be an example. So this is actually happening in medicine right now. So, you know, is a given treatment going to work or not? Well, it kind of depends. And there's lots of other factors involved and so forth. And the bot may never get good enough to really give you a definitive answer.
> 现在你开始明白了，对吧？因为这样一来，你得到了双方最聪明的答案，然后你作为一个人可以理解两个论点的逻辑，然后你可以在最后做出价值判断。我认为这可能是大多数事情在那一边发生的情况。否则你必须找到某种方法来训练这些东西，对吧？所以这里有一个例子。这其实在医学中正在发生。那么，某种治疗是否会有效呢？嗯，这有点依赖于具体情况。还有很多其他因素参与其中等等。而且机器人可能永远无法好到真的给你一个明确的答案。

[(2:36:30)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9390)
And so maybe what you want to do is you want to get a panel of the world's leading human doctors together and have them give the definitive answer. So the bot gets to be at least as good as they are. But does that get you all the way to the ultimate answer every time? Probably not because those human doctors probably were wrong about a bunch of stuff because it's a complicated topic that they're talking about. So there's this giant fuzzy middle where you still, as a human,  you have to decide what you want to get out of it. You have to decide like, okay, do I have values? What are my moral intuitions? How do I feel about this? How much risk do I want to take in my life?
> 所以也许你想做的就是找一组世界顶尖的医生一起给出明确答案。所以机器人至少要和他们一样优秀。但这是否每次都能让你得到最终答案呢？可能不会，因为那些医生可能对很多事情都是错误的，因为这是一个复杂的话题。所以有一个巨大的模糊地带，你作为一个人，仍然必须决定你想从中获得什么。你必须决定，好的，我是否有价值观？我的道德直觉是什么？我对这件事的感觉是什么？我在生活中愿意承受多大风险？

[(2:37:08)](https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/8033626?locate=9428)
Medical treatments, the bot can tell you if you take this treatment, which is much more invasive,  it'll probably cure you, but it might kill you. And, you know, you do this other thing and you'll, you know, you're almost certainly going to die,  but probably, you know, whatever, but you're not, whatever, whatever. And like, there's a value judgment that you have to make in that, that the thing can't answer. And so I think,  I think most of the important questions in our lives are going to be the ones that we still have to answer,  but we'll have, we'll have the AI help us.
> 医疗治疗，机器人可以告诉你如果你选择这个更具侵入性的治疗，它可能会治愈你，但也可能会致命。还有，你知道，你做这个其他的事情，你几乎肯定会死亡，但可能，随便吧，但你不，随便什么的。而且，在这件事上你必须做出的价值判断是机器人无法回答的。所以我认为，我们生活中大多数重要的问题仍然是我们必须回答的那些。但是我们会让人工智能帮助我们。
